id=\"module-position-PzSybOj-vTM\" class=\"story-asset oembed-asset\"><div class=\"story-oembed-wrap \"><div \n        class=\"js-oembed story-oembed story-oembed-usa-today story-oembed-type-link\"\n        data-oembed-type=\"link\"\n        data-oembed-provider=\"usa-today\"><style>\n    .oembed-asset-link { border-bottom: 1px solid #e1e1e1; }\n    .oembed-link-anchor { display: block; clear: both; }\n    p.oembed-link-desc { font-size: 100%; color: #666; font-weight: normal; margin: 0 14px 14px 14px; font-family: 'Futura Today Light'; text-align: left; line-height: 120%; }\n</style><div class=\"oembed-asset oembed-asset-link oembed-asset-usa-today oembed-simple-link-container\"><a href=\"http://www.usatoday.com/story/news/world/2017/03/15/trump-travel-ban-targeting-muslim-countries-facing-multiple-court-hearings/99203270/\" data-track-label=\"newrecircinline\" class=\"oembed-simple-link oembed-link-anchor\"><p class=\"oembed-link-desc\">Trump slams federal judge&#39;s freeze on second travel ban</p><div style=\"clear: both;\"></div></a></div></div></div></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>At the lawn of the Metro courthouse, thousands of protesters jeered as the president arrived in downtown Nashville. Inside the 1960s era arena, multiple protesters interrupted Trump's speech and were escorted out \u2014 including one woman holding a sign that read, \"Medicare for all.\"</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Trump's loyalists responded with chants of \"Trump!\" and \"USA!\" that were akin to his many stump speeches last year.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Trump began his afternoon in Nashville at The Hermitage, historic home of Jackson, the nation's seventh president whose populist appeal has drawn comparison to Trump.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\u201cHe understood that great leadership was about putting America First,\" Trump said shortly after taking the stage for his rally. \u201cIt\u2019s time that America heard your voice, and believe me, on November 8, they heard your voice.\u201d</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Trump proceeded to tout his accomplishments, ticking off several of the deeds he considers his early crowning achievements:</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><strong>\u2022 </strong>Pulling out of the Trans-Pacific Partnership trade deal.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><strong>\u2022\u00a0</strong>Promoting the construction of the Dakota pipeline.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><strong>\u2022\u00a0</strong>Touting improving job numbers.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><strong>\u2022\u00a0</strong>Progressing with plans to build the border wall.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><strong>\u2022\u00a0</strong>Deregulation \u2014 he spent Wednesday morning in Detroit, signaling is administration would move away form fuel-efficiency standards set by the Obama administration.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div id=\"module-position-PzSybOjV0oI\" class=\"story-asset image-asset\"><aside itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" class=\"wide single-photo\"><img itemprop=\"url\" src=\"http://www.gannett-cdn.com/-mm-/07b86fd70e142d3dc4e28e199a863a94f0bfb3ab/c=347-0-4302-2974&amp;r=x408&amp;c=540x405/local/-/media/2017/03/15/TennGroup/Nashville/636251942442515306--04A1622.JPG\" alt=\"President Donald Trump arrives at Nashville International\" width=\"540\" height=\"405\" data-mycapture-src=\"\"\n                    data-mycapture-sm-src=\"\" /><meta itemprop=\"name\" content=\"NAS-Trump\" /><meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"405\" /><meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"540\" /><p>President Donald Trump arrives at Nashville International Airport  Wednesday, March 15, 2017 in Nashville, Tenn.<meta itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\" content=\"Andrew Nelles / The Tennessean\" />&nbsp;<span class=\"credit\">(Photo: Andrew Nelles / The Tennessean)</span></p></aside><div class=\"clearfix\"></div></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\u201cAnd we have just gotten started,\" Trump said. \"Wait to you see what\u2019s coming, folks.\u201d</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Trump then made his case for a travel ban that a federal judge in Hawaii had halted moments before the president took the stage. It marked third judicial decision that has gone against the president's attempt to stop refugees and some immigrants from entering the county.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\u201cLet me give you the bad, the sad news. Moments ago, I learned that a district judge in Hawaii \u2014 part of the much overturned 9th Circuit Court \u2014 and I have to be nice, otherwise I\u2019ll be criticized,\u201d Trump said.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\u201cA judge has just blocked our executive order on travel and refugees coming in to our country from certain countries,\" he said. \"The order blocked was a watered-down version of the first order.\u201d</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Trump vowed to fight for the plan, appealing the ruling to the U.S. Supreme Court if necessary, while floating the idea of re-issuing the original ban. That order barred travel from seven majority Muslim countries and was already halted by two different judicial orders.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Leading up to Trump's speech, health care had been expected to be the focus, but he didn't approach the issue until nearly a half-hour into his remarks.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\"The bill that I will ultimately sign will get rid of Obamacare and make health care better for you and your family,\" Trump said.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div id=\"module-position-PzSybOjtiAs\" class=\"story-asset image-asset\"><aside itemprop=\"associatedMedia\" itemscope itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ImageObject\" class=\"wide single-photo\"><img itemprop=\"url\" src=\"http://www.gannett-cdn.com/-mm-/6227472b7d658352b483d9b261bcdaef6945b12f/c=46-0-4408-3280&amp;r=x408&amp;c=540x405/local/-/media/2017/03/15/TennGroup/Nashville/636251816165444271--ELA7787.JPG\" alt=\"Merchandise is for sale outside Municipal Auditorium\" width=\"540\" height=\"405\" data-mycapture-src=\"\"\n                    data-mycapture-sm-src=\"\" /><meta itemprop=\"name\" content=\"NAS-Trump\" /><meta itemprop=\"height\" content=\"405\" /><meta itemprop=\"width\" content=\"540\" /><p>Merchandise is for sale outside Municipal Auditorium where President Donald Trump will hold a rally Wednesday, March 15, 2017 in Nashville, Tenn.<meta itemprop=\"copyrightHolder\" content=\"Lacy Atkins / The Tennessean\" />&nbsp;<span class=\"credit\">(Photo: Lacy Atkins / The Tennessean)</span></p></aside><div class=\"clearfix\"></div></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>While providing few specifics, Trump acknowledged some of the procedural hurdles still facing the House GOP's bill. He promised additional phases of health care reform without going in to specifics. He also alluded to recent decisions of the health care companies BlueCross BlueShield and Humana to pull out of Obamacare markets in Tennessee.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start (Photo: George Walker IV / The Tennessean)\n\nNASHVILLE \u2014 President Trump touted his first 60 days in office as the most productive ever for a president and compared himself to President Andrew Jackson during a raucous rally Wednesday in Nashville that resembled the campaign that catapulted him into office.\n\nDrawing roars from the thousands in attendance, Trump slammed a Hawaii federal judge\u2019s decision earlier in the day that temporarily halted the administration\u2019s new attempt to ban most travel from six majority Muslim countries.\n\nHe also threw his support behind a House Republican effort to overhaul Obamacare and vowed additional changes of his own.\n\n\u201cIt\u2019s time for us to embrace our glorious national destiny,\u201d Trump said at the conclusion of his 40-minute speech.\n\nTrump took the stage Wednesday evening later than expected as long lines of supporters waited in the cold to get into the arena because of a security bottleneck and confusion.\n\nAt the lawn of the Metro courthouse, thousands of protesters jeered as the president arrived in downtown Nashville. Inside the 1960s era arena, multiple protesters interrupted Trump's speech and were escorted out \u2014 including one woman holding a sign that read, \"Medicare for all.\"\n\nTrump's loyalists responded with chants of \"Trump!\" and \"USA!\" that were akin to his many stump speeches last year.\n\nTrump began his afternoon in Nashville at The Hermitage, historic home of Jackson, the nation's seventh president whose populist appeal has drawn comparison to Trump.\n\n\u201cHe understood that great leadership was about putting America First,\" Trump said shortly after taking the stage for his rally. \u201cIt\u2019s time that America heard your voice, and believe me, on November 8, they heard your voice.\u201d\n\nTrump proceeded to tout his accomplishments, ticking off several of the deeds he considers his early crowning achievements:\n\n\u2022 Pulling out of the Trans-Pacific Partnership trade deal.\n\n\u2022 Promoting the construction of the Dakota pipeline.\n\n\u2022 Touting improving job numbers.\n\n\u2022 Progressing with plans to build the border wall.\n\n\u2022 Deregulation \u2014 he spent Wednesday morning in Detroit, signaling is administration would move away form fuel-efficiency standards set by the Obama administration.\n\nPresident Donald Trump arrives at Nashville International Airport Wednesday, March 15, 2017 in Nashville, Tenn. (Photo: Andrew Nelles / The Tennessean)\n\n\u201cAnd we have just gotten started,\" Trump said. \"Wait to you see what\u2019s coming, folks.\u201d\n\nTrump then made his case for a travel ban that a federal judge in Hawaii had halted moments before the president took the stage. It marked third judicial decision that has gone against the president's attempt to stop refugees and some immigrants from entering the county.\n\n\u201cLet me give you the bad, the sad news. Moments ago, I learned that a district judge in Hawaii \u2014 part of the much overturned 9th Circuit Court \u2014 and I have to be nice, otherwise I\u2019ll be criticized,\u201d Trump said.\n\n\u201cA judge has just blocked our executive order on travel and refugees coming in to our country from certain countries,\" he said. \"The order blocked was a watered-down version of the first order.\u201d\n\nTrump vowed to fight for the plan, appealing the ruling to the U.S. Supreme Court if necessary, while floating the idea of re-issuing the original ban. That order barred travel from seven majority Muslim countries and was already halted by two different judicial orders.\n\nLeading up to Trump's speech, health care had been expected to be the focus, but he didn't approach the issue until nearly a half-hour into his remarks.\n\n\"The bill that I will ultimately sign will get rid of Obamacare and make health care better for you and your family,\" Trump said.\n\nMerchandise is for sale outside Municipal Auditorium where President Donald Trump will hold a rally Wednesday, March 15, 2017 in Nashville, Tenn. (Photo: Lacy Atkins / The Tennessean)\n\nWhile providing few specifics, Trump acknowledged some of the procedural hurdles still facing the House GOP's bill. He promised additional phases of health care reform without going in to specifics. He also alluded to recent decisions of the health care companies BlueCross BlueShield and Humana to pull out of Obamacare markets in Tennessee.\n\n\"Insurers are fleeing,\" Trump said. \"It's a
